text:
Before I even read the reviews I realised that 2 TABLESPOONS of Baking Powder was obviously a typo for this recipe. I used 2 TEASPOONS like others, and this recipe turned out so light and fluffy! I also omitted the oil as I'm not a fan of extra fat in my pancakes. I halved the sugar and served them with real grade 3 maple syrup and they were so light and tasty.

text:
I've read all the other reviews, and for those who said they were flat and aweful, you must have mixed them for too long! I've made the recipe AS IS several times, and let the batter rest for 5 minutes and they were SO fluffy and tastey. I have also made them with a little vanilla and that added a super flavor! So, beat your egg, people, and mix your dry ingredients together, and you won't have to mix and mix the batter. Just mix until blended, and let it rest a bit before you cook them and they will be great!!!

2c flour 
3 teaspoons of baking powder
2 3/4 of milk 
4 Tablespoons of veg oil
2 eggs 
1/4 c sugar 

They came out very nice!!!

text:
This is a great recipe. Especially while most of us are trying to cut back on spending at the market. Beats Bisquick any day! My boys want pancakes every weekend and we tried this recipe. My son Travis, (15), is quite the cook. He made a few changes. We doubled the recipe, 2 cups of flour, 4 level teaspoons of baking powder, 1 teaspoon salt,   1 teaspoon vanilla, 2 eggs (beaten), 4 tablespoons of sugar, 4 tablespoons of veg.oil, then gradually added 1-1/2 cups of half & half. Let it sit for a few minutes, to rise. Perfect Pancakes! Moist & Fluffy. Thanks!

text:
I have finally found a recipe that came out great for pancakes! I did what other reviewers suggested and cut the baking powder down to 2 tsp. added vanilla and cut the salt to 1/2 tsp also used butter instead of oil. I used 50/50 White and Wheat flour and they had great texture!! kids loved them and husband. I noticed other reviews had problems with too thin or runny, I don't know if this makes a difference but a couple things: Mix dry and wet ingredients separately and then mix well together Make sure pan is hot but not too hot like medium low heat, cast iron pan works really well. Don't grease the pan too much it will make the batter even thinner.  Just a few tips that made mine turn out great!!

I give these pancakes a four, with some changes.  I followed the recommendation of 2tsp baking powder.  I also added 2T brown sugar instead of white, a tsp of cinnamon, and I added a tsp (and a bit more) of vanilla.  (Many reviewers cut back on the salt, but I thought they tasted fine with the amount shown in the recipe.  I also added chocolate chips to half the cakes.  The flavor after these modifications was great, however, the texture left a bit to be desired.  I thought these took a bit too much elbow grease to cut into.  I may try add a bit more baking powder to see if that fluffs them up a bit, hopefully without altering the flavor.  Overall, these taste good in a pinch!

If you let the batter rest for 5 minutes or so before you start cooking it, the baking powder will have time to activate.  Without the rest time, you'll end up with a runny batter that's hard to control on the griddle.  The pancakes could use some extra flavor from buttermilk or vanilla, or fruit added to the pancake while it cooks.  Overall, this is a decent basic pancake recipe.

I originally was going to make another pancake recipe from this site but then I saw the video for Easy Pancakes and decided to make them instead. The video states to use 2 tbsp of baking powder but I used 2 tsp instead, as written in the recipe (I didn't want that baking powder aftertaste). These turned really good and my kids loved them! They weren't too fluffy, nor too flat, and it was really quick to prepare. I will definitely make this recipe again the next time my kids ask for pancakes on a weekday and I don't feel like spending so much time in the kitchen making breakfast on a weekday! text:
These pancakes are so good - if anyone thinks a box mix is easier they are wrong - taste is everything and these beat the pants off any box mix - let it sit after stiring and the mix will rise and the texture will get fluffy, then stir again before putting the batter in the pan - it seems to do something because this is a thick mix (supposed to be) so if your are used to a box mix the texture will throw you off at first, but  anyway REAL MAPLE syrup rules, so use it.  Also, I add freshly whipped cream on top of these pancakes - that is easy too - just whip (on high or med-high) some heavy cream for a few minutes and you'll have fresh whipped cream :)

text:
this is an ok recipe but for those of us that live in fairly high altitude you may fine this very runny and come out more like crepes. 
So here are a few tips I use to thicken it up.
one cut down the milk to 3/4 cups or increase the flour by 1/3 cup (more depending how high up on mountains you are)  
Also wait AT least 10 minutes after mixing everything before putting it on the pan (best results is to make this the night before)
I also find when you pour the batter on the pan it's best to lift the pan off the stove top and let it take it's shape before putting it back on top. It helps from the batter running to the edges and makes it more round.
and I also just like adding a teaspoon of vanilla for a little extra flavor. and real maple syrup is always preferred ;)

text:
For anyone not too experienced in the kitchen, take note:  This recipe makes only about 3 large pancakes.  You will need to double it if you are feeding more that one or two people.  It is a very good recipe, though.  I was looking for an easy pancake recipe that wasn't too hard to do first thing out of bed.  This is it!  I followed the other reviewer's recommendations and decreased the baking powder to 2 TEAspoons, and added a bit of vanilla.  I toss it all in a large mason jar and SHAKE.  then I just pour it into the pan.  Perfect every time.

text:
The main issue with this recipe is the lack of an acid. That's why so many of the reviewers cut down on the baking soda.  Solution: Buttermilk.   I used the allotted amount of baking soda, and replaced the milk with buttermilk. The cakes rose beautifully, and tasted nothing like baking soda.  You could also have added a tablespoon or so of white vinegar or lemon juice to regular milk to get the same affect.

text:
I love this recipe.  I would give it a five if not for the baking soda typo and the high salt content.  Thusfar, I have used this with regular flour and 1/2 whole wheat flour.  Next time, I plan to try self rising flour and omitting the salt and baking powder.  If you use regular flour, just add a pinch of salt and 2 tsp of baking powder.  It tastes great with cinnamon and vanilla extract.
Once I got distracted by my children and I didn't use cinnamon and vanilla extract and they were very bland.  Another mistake I made was to let our children over-stir the batter which made it very runny.  This recipe is much better than a box mix and just think:  If you use your own ingredients everything you've added you can pronounce!

text:
Not a bad recipe, but I think the point of a great recipe is that you don't have to alter it to make it palatable. 
If you reduce the salt a bit (1/2t or so), cut down the amount of baking powder drastically (about 3/4 tbsp), and add some cinnamon for flavor it's not a bad recipe at all - I imagine it would be a good base for some banana nut or cinnamon apple pancakes with the addition of the cinnamon. They weren't the best pancakes I've ever had but considering that Bisquick consistently lets me down with awful pancakes (I don't know how I know how to cook, yet I mess up box mix consistently!), it's an improvement.

A good start but it's not quite there yet as many reviewers have already noted.  I read all the reviews and reduced both the baking powder (3/4 T) and salt (pinch). I also added 1 teaspoon of vanilla extract and the rind of half an orange.  (Buy a Microplane!)  The pancakes had a nice hint of orange taste and were light and fluffy as well.

My husband and I both find this recipe pretty delicious! They are super restaurant-style fluffy! I would suggest adding a bit less baking powder, because I find they kinda fall apart when you use the full 2 tablespoons. Yes, they are a bit plain, but that's the great thing about them, you can add any flavor! I've tried cinnamon, fruit, chocolate chips. And they are so simple. This is a great basic recipe that is  great for a Sunday morning!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
These pancakes are the best Ive ever made. It goes great with chocolate chips, but you need to cut up berries/fruits before putting the in, or else they will stick out, and when you flip them, there will be a small ring around the fruit that is not cooked through. I always put the stove on medium for the first couple pancakes, and when it finally gets to its peak temp, I turn it down to low. My oven, however, always gets hotter than I tell it to, so maybe my stove just gets hotter than its supposed to. I noticed som other reviews saying there was way too much baking powder, and thats because there was a typo that said you should put in 2tbsp instead of 2tsp, but thats been fixed. In conclusion, these are the BEST youll ever find, try it.

Oh yeah, unless you are using pure maple syrup, look at the list of ingredients on the back. Theres probably a 99% chance the first, second or third ingredient in either corn syrup, or high fructose corn syrup. Both ingredients are absolutely TERRIBLE for you, and you should eat the least amount possible. Look it up. Sorry if this was too long and boring, 
ChickenLover

I admit I did not 'make' this recipe..... I've been making pancakes 'from scratch' for 60 years - but I would like to give you all a couple of tips.  Put some vinegar or lemon into the milk ahead of time and let it sit (1-2 tsp) - you will then have 'buttermilk'
which will make the pancakes much fluffier. Also, instead of 2 Tbsps. of oil or butter.....use melted bacon grease!  Provides great flavour & Vanilla is a good idea too.

text:
I was looking for an easy tasty pancake recipe and  stumbled across this. I typically made coconut pancakes, but was looking for more of the 'real' thing without the bad feeling afterwards. I made these GLuten Free and substituted the All Purpose GF flour. It measures cup for cup the same as regular flour. I doubled the recipe for 2 adults & 2 teens, but clearly needed to triple it. I did make a few changes based on the reviews. I only added 1/2tsp of salt per recipe, added 1/2 tsp of vanilla per recipe, substituted unsweetened Vanilla Almond milk and added real butter instead of the oil. I also made an easy homemade syrub to top them and we loved them. Will definitely be making these again.

text:
These pancakes were great! As with all recipes, I looked through several recipes and made my own modified version based from the original. I think that this made the perfect, most fluffy pancakes I have ever made. I cut down the salt amount to 1/2 a teaspoon, I added 1 teaspoon of vanilla extract, and I put in 3 tablespoons of softened butter instead of putting oil in the batter. To prevent my pan from getting sticky or burned, I kept drizzling the pan with oil while making the pancakes whenever I felt like the pan was getting too dry. I made two pancakes at a time, and even added fresh slices of strawberries inside some of them. After adding rasberry syrup and some with powdered sugar, my family and I couldn't get our hands off it!

text:
I am giving this five stars because it ended up being the perfect recipe for the problem that I had.  There was no baking powder in the house!  After researching substitutes for baking powder I used 1/4 tsp baking soda + 1/2 c buttermilk (which, amazingly, I had left over after making a batch of ranch dressing).  Also used 1/2 tsp salt and 1/2 tsp baking soda instead of the full tsp of salt.  Since I used the 1/2 cup buttermilk, I cut the regular milk to 1/2 c.  And used melted butter instead of oil.  Oils, other than peanut oil, in these types of recipes always taste like petroleum to me.  And, I griddle in butter.  Ended up with 12 approximately 3-1/2 " in diameter, slightly chewy (which, I love - I detest pancakes that crumble!), beautifully raised pancakes that did not have that baking powder taste (guess these are reasons why I am not particularly fond of biscuits).  Sorry for the long review, but am thrilled, after all of these years, I can now make a pancake that I love.

It gets gobbled down in no time flat whenever I make it, especially for a bunch of hungry church folks, and hard working guys! My advice to get thee fluffiest pancake you can get with this recipe is to whisk the ingredients together and let stand for about 5 minutes or so. The batter will start to bubble and when you pour it they will fluff right up!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
These pancakes apparently got a bad rap 'cause of an initial typo in qty of baking powder, which has been corrected. As written now, they are perfectly delicious & easy to make, & should be just as or even more moist & flavorful than the much-higher-rated "Good Old Fashioned" due to proportionately less baking powder, more sugar & more milk! That said, I still found these (as well as the "Old Fashioned") too salty, so I reduce the salt by half. These are my very picky 7yo granddaughter's fave pancakes, & the following are her fave modifications (dairy-free & healthier): 1/2 cup home-ground oats (or oat or buckwheat flour) & 1/2 cup white whole wheat flour; melted butter-sub (Earth Balance, which I melt in frying pan, thus "greasing" pan at same time); 1/2 tsp salt; soy or almond milk; & xylitol, brown sugar or maple syrup (yum!). With the oats (or buckwheat) & white whole wheat, they still come out fluffy, yet have a delicious flavor! I like these better than the "Good Old Fashioned" 'cause the higher milk & sweetener make them so flavorful, she doesn't even add syrup; just eats them straight out of hand! (They are also good as a snack in her lunch box.) Oh, & with oats or buckwheat for half of flour, don't need to worry as much about overworking dough & activating gluten, since there is so much less of it. One last point: I add butter to cold milk while butter is still sizzling, & haven't noticed any problem with "cold" milk that way. These truly are "EASY" & great!

text:
Seriously the best pancake recipe ever!  I have tried waiting and not waiting the hour. I really prefer not waiting. They remind me of cracker barrel pancakes, but I also made them smaller like McDonald's. I wait to add the blueberries until I pour it in my cast iron skillet. This recipe is crazy versatile. I have experimented with different fruits and even made tropical coconut pancakes. Sometimes I add flax seeds, sunflower seeds, or oatmeal and cinnamon. I also made smaller sizes to make little breakfast sandwiches to freeze for mornings when I'm in a hurry.  I'm in Florida so of course I had to key lime it up!  Added a little lime juice, coconut and topped with a little cream cheese coolwhip mixture. Thanks Alison for sharing Todd's recipe!!

text:
Nice basic recipe. I took others' suggestion to reduce baking powder to two teaspoons.  Made a couple of my own variations to "healthen" them up - so ended up with something quite different I guess. Substituted 1/4 cup of oatmeal for part of the flour. And used a quarter cup of prune juice I'm trying to get rid of for part of the milk (for the rest I used almond milk). Added a bit of grated coconut, chopped walnuts and blueberries because that's what I had in the kitchen, plus a dash of cinnamon. Topped with honey. These are actually pretty darn good, with a good balance of lightness and heartiness.  You can't really taste the prune juice, it just comes across as vague fruitiness.

I used this recipe for a breakfast bake. The only things I did different were that I used 1/3 C whole wheat flour and 2/3 C white flour, I added 1 tsp vanilla and I cut back on the salt. text:
I made this recipe and they turned out pretty bad, my kids wouldn't eat them and just spit them back out. So I made my own adjustments, 2cups ap flour, 2 tsp b. powder, 1 tsp salt/sugar, 1 1/4 cup milk, room temp, 1 egg room temp, 3 tbsp melted butter and 1 tbsp vanilla. Sift dry ingreidents together twice, then mix all wet together, making sure milk and egg is at room temp, then add wet to dry, mix well...pour on griddle until small bubbles form, then flip and you have better than bisquick! Makes about 10 md size pancakes.

text:
I gave this one a 4, because I knew off the bat that (like others) I would have to reduce the baking powder and the salt.  I used 2 tsp baking powder and 2 pinches of salt.  This is actually a really good basic recipe otherwise.  For the people who found the batter runny and added more flour, eh.  That probably turned them in a near-brick doughy pancake.  The baking powder is actually what makes pancakes light and fluffy, and mine turned out just fine.  If you are having problems with pancakes being tough and thin, try stirring them more gently and not as long.  The only other changes that I made were to use whole wheat flour and honey instead of sugar for my own nutritional desires.

As is, this recipe's measurements are off. I knew that two tablespoons of baking powder would be too much as would
a whole tsp. of salt. I reduced the baking powder to two teaspoons and cut 
the salt in half. I also added a bit of 
vanilla flavoring and used buttermilk,
as I had some that was about to turn.

This recipe makes eight medium pancakes,
enough for our breakfast with some leftover to freeze for busy mornings. 
They turned out like a basic pancake, no
frills.

text:
Seems like a nice basic recipe. While I prefer buttermilk-based pancakes, I was out of anything to fake-make buttermilk (no vinegar, lemon juice, cream of tartar - it was sad), so I tried this recipe with the previous recommendations of using 2 tsp. (not tbsp.) of baking powder, 1 pinch of salt, and adding 1 tsp. of vanilla and a dash of cinnamon. I made two batches, one plain and one with mini chocolate chips, and both were very good. The batter did well after sitting for a few minutes while the griddle heated. Beware the serving recommendations - I was able to get about 8 4 inch chocolate chip pancakes out of the 4 serving settings, when I doubled it for the plain I got about 12 (the chips obviously added some bulk).

region:

country:
None
text:
This recipe was indeed very easy and tasty, an appreciable feature when you're a student or otherwise time constrained. With a large griddle you can easily be done cooking in under a half hour. This recipe is also a very good base that can easily be modified to your liking. Myself, I like adding a friendly dash of nutmeg and cloves to mine. As well I think that using 1/2 whole wheat flour give the pancakes a rich and tasty flavour, without compromise. Using brown sugar instead of one of the tablespoons is also a nice touch (flowing raw sugar is best to ensure it blends well). Finally, displacing a bit of the flour  (1 tblspoon) with brown rice flour ensures a nice smooth texture and also gives them a slightly more even colour.

I like this recipe, it's easy, and uses things you keep on hand. I like being able to provide breakfast when "there's nothing to eat in the house". I think it really doesn't need quite so much baking powder, the dough rises in the bowl between pours, and you have to stir and add more milk as you go.
